O, sons, when I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, by its completion in it, and by its expositions and declarations, it has become clear to me that you will complete with this treatise, which is a part of the action by hand, i.e., surgery.
For the action by hand is prohibited in our realm and in our time is deprived of all prestige, while greatly risking the science of it, and its traces are obscured; and nothing remains of it except a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which they altered and led to those errors and hesitations that closed their minds to it and diminished its strength and skill.
And it has become clear to me that I will animate this through the arrangement of this treatise in that second way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and so that it might come with the forms of the tools of cauterization and other instruments of the work as is fitting for addition of the declaration, and for preparation of it, which cause is necessary.
But the cause for which there is no good craftsman by hand in our time is because the art of medicine is long, and that its practitioner must be practiced beforehand in the science of anatomy, which recognizes Gaulish in that it knows the joints of the members and their forms, and the connection and separation of them; and have the knowledge of bones, nerves, and tendons, and the number of those, and their emanation.
And so Hypocras says that by name is much, but in the work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
But we have already said that in the introduction to this book; for whomever is not learned what we have said of anatomy, it is not permitted that they might fall into error by which men will die, as I have seen too many of those, for some are formed in this science and throw themselves from it without experience.
For I saw a foolish and experienced physician pierce a scrophula on the neck of a woman, and piercing some arteries of the neck so that much blood flowed and the woman died in his arms.
And I saw another physician who extracted a stone from a man who had proceeded in his state, and the stone was large, and he came to him and drew out that stone with a piece of the bladder, and that man died on the third day.
And I had called to extract it, and I saw that for the size of the stone and for the disposition of the patient over him that he would die.
And I saw another physician who took stipends from a duke of our land for surgery, and there came to him a broken black slave; and preparing with his ignorance, he extracted the fracture over the plague with powders and splints with strong compression, and did not allow the wound air.
And then he discharged it according to his desires, and then bound it, and then let it remain for some days and commanded that we loosen the dressing; and it became so that the thigh and leg were pustularized, and came to ruin.
And I was called to him, and prepared to loosen the dressing, and achieved tranquility and eased of his pains.
But however, corruption was confirmed in the member, so that I could not restrain it and the corruption did not cease wandering in the member as the patient perished.
And I saw another physician who pierced a cankerous ulcer, and was ulcerated for some days, as the wickedness of it increased with its lord.
The cause of which is that the cold choler is pure, and then it does not come to him from iron at all, but that there be some member suffering from it.
And so, sons, it is necessary for you that the action by hand be divided into two divisions: one is in operation to him who is associated with health, and the other is in work with which there is peril in the major dispositions.
And I have already discussed that in every chapter of this book in which there appears operation in which there is error and fear; so that it is necessary for you to guard against that and leave it, so that the foolish might not hinder your way and disgraced you.
And thus take up your arms with solicitude and the protection of God, and your patients with gentleness and firmness.
And use the better way by the grace of God and to bring about health and praiseworthy success, and lay aside the terrible diseases of difficult cure, and take up your arms from what makes you fearful so that solicitude in your faith and in your name does not escape you: for it remains to your glory, and more in the world and beyond to your saintliness.
Gaulish has already said in some of his books: "Do not heal evil ill, so that bad physicians are not named."
And I have divided this book according to three chapters.
Begins the division of the book, and first of the first part. The first chapter ordered from the head into feet, in the forms of the instruments and the tools of cauterization, and what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, of bleeding and piercing, and of cupping, and of plagues, and of extraction of arrows and like things, all chaptered and ordered from the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, of restoration and of dislocation, and of cure of torque and like things; chaptered from the head into feet, and of the forms of the instruments.
We will say the quality of the humors of that cauterization and of the pains of it, and in what condition cauterization is prohibited.
So I say that the speech of the quality of the humor of cauterization and the pain of it is long speech and prolix, and subtle by science, and secret hidden; and many have spoken greatly of it, and from it are disagreed, and for me a little of their speeches suffices, fearing prolixity.
And so I say that cauterization confers to all universal complexions, which are by matter or without matter, excepting two complexions, which are complexions of phlegm without matter.
In the complexions phlegmy and dry with matter discorded; for some said that cauterization is beneficial to it, and others said the contrary of that, that cauterization is not convenient in ill of which is by quality and dryness, for the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and inconvenient that ill of which is phlegmy and dry be healed.
And he said the contrary of that, that by cauterization is made humor in all ill which is phlegmy and dry that one sees in the bodies of men, for when you compare the body of man and his humors to the complexions of fire, you rub the body of man dry.
And I say by the speech of that, that experiment that to me some times have discovered.
However, let the one who comes to this topic not be ignorant of what is already written and practiced in the chapter on cautery by various authors, and has understood the diversity of human complexions and the disposition of diseases in their bodies, and their causes, and their accidents, and the space of time of them.
But in other complexions you should not be afraid, especially in wet and damp diseases, for all doctors have agreed about them and are not in disagreement that cautery is beneficial for those.
And know, children, that the secret of healing by cautery with fire and its goodness is that cautery with burning medicine is that fire is simple, whose action only affects the part being cauterized and does not affect another part except for a little harm.
But the action of burning medicine reaches all parts, and strongly brings about a difficult-to-cure disease in the part it affects, and strongly helps it.
But fire, by its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that except that it expels the surplus. And it is known to us through experiment and through the length of service in the study of art upon the truth of causes; and because of this I am excused from the length of speech. And if it were not that my free time was not read in this pause, a secret hidden from you by fire, and the quality of its action on bodies and its expulsion by which you expel diseases, with philosophical speech demonstrated, which would be acute in your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree on the time when it is convenient to perform cautery, and pause in the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, in order that the harm by the accidental time is submerged in the benefit of what is drawn by cautery, and especially if cautery is for pains or necessary pains, strong and feverish, which do not endure delay so that malice does not come, which is greater than a little harm due to the passage of time.
And therefore do not wonder in your minds, children, that this is not considered except by the common people and foolish doctors; it is that for that disease which is healed by cautery, there is no reduction of time at all, and they pause in that consequence.
And the cause is not as they think, for cautery is not but in the place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries up the moisture which are the cause by which pains come.
But cautery surpasses medicine in power of its strength and value of its action, and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that the disease may return at some time according to the complexion of the patient and the location of his disease, and the strength of it, and what is prepared in his body from the aggregation of surpluses in him, and what comes to him in his acquisition in food and likeness of these causes; unless the disease for which cautery was administered was a subtle disease in a part of few surpluses and moisture, so that cautery for pain and its likeness in it, it is possible that the pain will not return in him, but this happens in small things.
But the vulgar saying is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is a true saying, not to what they understand about it, for they believe that there is no cure that benefits from medicine or any other cause except cautery.
And the cause is contrary to that; and the intention that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is not but when we administer remedies in some diseases, and those medicines do not confer, and at the end of the cause we administer a man cautery, and it benefits for that. And from here we understand that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the intention which the vulgar and foolish doctors understand.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and subtlety of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not do that, unless it is absolutely true, for I have already proven and proven to you that this is not but in some bodies without the others, and cautery with it is good and better than with iron as they said; but when you perform cautery with fire with gold, it is not declared to you, for it is ignited according to the quantity that you want due to the redness of gold, and because it prepares to receive friction; and if you apply an igniter over it, gold melts by the fire, and some sheets fall into the fire so that the craftsman catches them due to the occupation of that.
And for this, cautery with iron is done more lightly and closer to the rightness of operation.
And I have ordered this chapter on cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head among the feet, so that I may ask for what I want from him.
The first chapter.
This cauterization confers to moisture and coldness above the servile accident of which there are two causes, it is the cause of soda and multitude of fluxes, called headache, from the parts of the temples and ears flowing, and multitude of sleeping, and toothache and of the jaw, and generally of all disease that comes by frigidity, as well as paralysis, stroke, and likeness in those diseases.
The form of this cauterization is this, that first of all you command the patient to be evacuated by laxative medicine, the head being washed clean, for three or four days according to the strength of the patient and his age and habit.
And then command him to shave his head with a razor, and then let him lie between your knees on a low bench and let him lie on his feet.
And then pause the edge of your palm palm up to the point above the nose between the eyes. But however, when your middle finger's location is reached, signal that location with the tip of the thumb and then ignite the olive cautery of which this is the form:
And then pause it on the marked location, in such a way that it descends, and your hand be constrained little by little, and you revolve it.
And then lift your hand lightly and look at the location, and if you see that some quantity of the head is already uncovered, as well as the quantity of hair, then lift your hand again, and if it has not returned to its original location with that iron, with another one, if it is cool, enter until it is seen by you that which I have said to you.
And then take a little salt and dissolve it over the location and let it be for three days.
And then pause on it cotton dipped in vinegar and let it be on it until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then heal the location with four-part thuốc long into it has healed.
And they said that when the Roman plaster is open, so many honeys are put in it, because it is better and more beneficial.
And they said that the jaw should be cauterized within the bone, and the cautery should be applied until some part of the substance of the bone is burnt.
And then scrape off what is burnt and then heal it.
Others said that the cautery arrived at the end, passing through the strong bone while the bone collapsed, and this is the form of small alphecati. And they believe that from that place, the vapors of the head expire.
And when there has been a wound open for a long time and it is cured while still unhealed,
But I have never seen these two species of cautery in anyone, except some people according to the way of fear; and that person, for me, is better off healthy than ill, because the head is devastated by the solution of its continuity with it as we have testified in other members, and especially when the patient's head is of a foul nature.
And the first kind of cautery is more safe and better for me; and that person uses it and works on that with health.
Chapter Second.
Of the cautery of the head
When in all the head there is chronic and long-lasting pain and this is prolonged in the patient, and he uses lances and cupping glasses and head purges and plasters and poultices and hot stones and bandages and similar things, and especially if he has already been cauterized by a cautery which did not help him for any of those causes, then consider that if the patient's head is of strong creation in its nature; and it is foul and finds great friction there, then cauterize it with another cautery under that one a little. And if it is necessary to cauterize under the head and it benefits him another form of cautery by which the wound is held, then cauterize with a cautery on the crown of his head where the scalp is split. The scalp is split and the amount we have measured is uncovered from the bone and that is cauterized with a cautery in the back part of the head at the place which is called a vein — and it is the place where the ventouse is placed. And put your hand on it, and do not uncover the bone, because the patient through that finds much more pain than from any other cautery of the head.
And I say that this cautery is in its place, because the cautery by which they cauterize the horns of the head and the occiput is more subtle cautery than that by which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is how it is done:
Chapter Third.
Of the cautery of non-ancient migration.
When a sudden pain is in the front of the head, or pain is stretched into the eye, the head must be evacuated by cleansing medicines, and other treatment must be administered, which I have written about in the beginnings of illnesses; and if all this does not help, cauterization of it is in two ways: either by acute burning medicine, or by iron.
But a cautery by burning medicine is that you take an onion, and cut it up and season the ends of it on both sides with salt. Then pierce the place of the pain in the temple with a pointed lance so that it penetrates under the scalp and is hidden.
Then tighten it with a binding bandage so that it presses down strongly and leave it there for three hours; then remove the onion and treat the wound with ointment, and leave the wound for two or three days, then put your hand over the place while immersing it in warm water so that the place becomes swollen.
Then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you want to do this with some other burning medicines which I have written about in the two tractates of burning medicines.
But the cauterization by iron according to this way: heat up an iron cautery and this is how it is done:
And it is called closed claw nail, because the head of it is like a nail with some curvature and in the middle part of it there is a small prominence.
Then put your hand over the place of the pain — so that the iron which is underneath is not burned — and move the iron little by little quickly.
And if the quantity of it which is burned by the thickness of the scalp is according to the size of it, and raise your hand so that the artery underneath is not burned which is underneath, so that there is no flow of blood.
Then dip the wound in salty water and put it on the place for three days; then put a bandage moistened with wine on it and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you want, cauterize with the tip of the scalpel according to cautery and beware of incision of artery in this non-ancient migration.
Chapter Fourth.
Of the cautery of ancient migration.
When you cure migration with what we have said about the previous treatment and what we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and the treatment does not help, and you see that for the illness which is not sufficient to it what we have said about the first cautery by medicine or the cautery by fire, then wherever you ignite the cautery-scalpel so that it turns white, measure on the place of the pain a length of line of which the size of the finger is, or whichever, and put your hand aside for a while and tighten it so that you pierce the artery and it comes into the bone.
However it is necessary for you to guard against the continuance of the jaw, which is worn down because of mastication, and that the vein not be burned and the nerve which controls it, and that no spasm come upon it.
And if it is about the custody and caution of flow of blood from the artery which is split, because in its splitting there is danger, and especially to him who ignores what he does and is unskilled and inexperienced; and leave the operation at the beginning.
And I will come with remembrance of the regimen of accidental flow of blood from the artery according to its way in this free book.
And if you see that this illness does not help this cautery and you see the body of the patient tolerable, cauterize it in the middle part of the head as we have measured, and cure the wound until it is healed.
And if you want to administer the cautery which we have said in the chapter of stretching of the artery with cautery having two points, and this cautery is better and more certain.
Chapter Fifth.
Of the cauterization of pains of auricles.
When in the auricle there is pain because of friction and it is cured by lancing and by the other treatment which I have said in the division, and the pain is not relieved, then ignite the cautery, and this is that one which has the name puncta, and this is how it is done:
Then pierce the ignition and let it be carried around all of the auricle as it is turned, or in the circuit of each of them if the pain is in any of them. Apply the cautery at the base of the ear slowly, little by little, until you have felt the area with the tip.
And if the cautery makes points on the entire ear, and he feels that, then cure the places inside which are healthy.
Chapter VI
Of cauterization by torture.
Torture which is cured and treated with cauterization is only of the humors which come from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses.
Avoid cauterization of the humors which come from dryness or from nervous spasms.
When you treat that kind of torture with poultices and clysters and washes, and your treatment doesn't work, then you should cauterize the patient in three places: the first at the base of the ear, the second a small spot below his temple, and the third at the junction of two lips.
And apply your cautery against the direction in which the illness is traveling, because softening will not come except through the part that appears to be healing.
And the way of cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cautery at the right side of the highest part of the ear, a little above the horn of the head; another at the temple, the length of which should be according to the length of the finger nail, and apply your hand with the cautery inside until the amount of the half of the size of a peppercorn is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery; it is a kind of scalpel, the shape of which is in front like a table. But indeed more subtle is that one little bit here and there; and where it cuts through excessive thickness a little.
And then cure the place with that which is in front processed until it is healed.
Chapter VII.
Of cauterization of old apoplexy.
When apoplexy is old and you treat it with what we have said and your treatment doesn't work and the patient doesn't have a fever, then cauterize that in four places: especially on all the horns of his head; and with cautery and the middle part of the head, as we have said; and with cautery in the groin. And the way of cauterization is done according to what is above the finger nail.
And indeed it has been cauterized on the mouth of the stomach; and that is the most rear; and indeed let it be cured with what processes.
Chapter VIII.
Of cauterization made for oblivion caused by phlegm.
Let the patient be given in the beginning large poultices and purging pills, the servant cleansing agents.
And then scrape the entire head of the patient and apply over the groin a poultice of cedar described in the treatise on poultices.
And apply that several times, for that is the way of cauterization. And do that according to the order of which I have already said.
And if he is healed by those, well and good; and if not, then do to him three cauterizations in the rear part of his head, which descend from the highest part of the head to the lowest part of the neck. And apply between each cautery the thickness of a finger nail, and then cure the cautery with that which it produces.
But if you feel an increase and the patient can tolerate it, then do to him cauterization in the middle part; and if you feel a greater increase, then cauterize that on both horns.
Then cure that until it is healed; and let the cautery be olive-colored according to the shape given before.
Chapter IX.
Of cauterization of parasites and of softening of all the body.
Let the patient be cleansed in cleansing of the head with poultices and with that which we have said; and then scrape the head of the patient, and then cauterize that with cautery in the middle part of the head, and with cautery on all the horns of the head, and with cautery on the rear part of him, and do to him three cauterizations on the spine of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the illness of softening of the body of trops and the illnesses tolerate that and the illness is strong, then cauterize that with four cauterizations on the spine of the neck, and lastly with cautery inside until the peppercorn mot of him burns, and raise your hand. Then cure that until it is healed; and let that be cauterized olive-colored.
Chapter X.
Of cauterization of epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless that epilepsy is caused by phlegm.
And therefore let the brain of him be cleansed at the beginning of his illness with herbs and with the other cure which we have said in the division when the patient is large and can tolerate the exception of medicines.
And if the patient is a child who does not suffer medicines, then administer to him washes and masticables, the servant cleansers, before the days pass, with the benefit of foods.
And then scrape the head of the patient, and then cauterize that with one cautery in the middle part of the head according to the previous way; and with another cautery on the back of his head, and on each horn of his head cauterize it. And if the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then cauterize that with cauteries which I have said, having paralysis and softening of the body on the spine of the neck and the spine of the back.
And let it be cauterized olive-colored according to how it was before.
But if the patient is a child, then apply a subtle cautery according to this way.
Chapter XI.
Of cauterization of melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humidity and phlegm, then cauterize that with the cauteries which we have said in the case of paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is excess of decline into melancholy, and the body of the patient is humid, then let him drink that which cleanses the brain of him according to what has preceded in the division.
And then scrape the head of the patient; and then make a turpentine decently made of pine resin over the circle, and then apply that to the middle part of the head.
Let the patient be in seclusion for sixty days, and let him be kept in all parts.
And then apply a poultice; and it is also worthy of being bled from the ear of sheep. And scorch that over fire with moderate heat according to measure, which he endures when it is within him. And now you will tie it in the middle of the head, in the circle, and loosen it so that it is relaxed.
And do this to the patient once a week, with the other treatment until he is healed; or if you wish, cauterize the area by making small points according to his pain, unless you have your hand on a cautery in such an order: this is a special cautery that moistens the brain equally.
Then put that cut in a soft bandage or gauze.
Chapter 12.
Of cauterization of water descending in the hole.
When to you is shown the beginning of water in the hole by the signs which I have said in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink that which purifies the head of him, and guard that from all moisture.
And do that sweat in a bath for a few days.
And now command him to wash his head, and cauterize that with a cautery in the middle of the head; and now cauterize that with two cauteries over two temples if there is the beginning of water in two holes, or on one side if there is the beginning of the water in one hole.
Cut with a cautery all the veins and arteries which are below the collar bone; and let the cauteries be in that length in the width of the temples.
And guard you from flows of blood when he is cauterized; and if you see flows of blood from him, stop it with some medicine which is possible to you.
And I come with wisdom which is in extraction of arteries and with incision of those and cauterization of flows of blood.
And sometimes he is cauterized in the neck below two bones with two cauteries recently produced.
Chapter 13.
Of cauterization of old tears.
When tears of the holes are ancient frequently and by the veins and arteries which are in the manifest location of the head outside and it is verified that this is superfluous flowing phlegmatic, then cauterize that with a cautery which we have recounted in the chapter of beginning of water falling into the holes, and with a cautery in the middle of the head and with two cauteries in the neck below two temples, and with two cauteries in the neck below two bones. And if there is need of addition, then cauterize that in all sides of the hole's mouth on the end of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Chapter 14.
Of cauterization of stink of nose.
When you heal him with that which we have said in the division and your healing does not help, then prepare and give the patient the clysters for three nights; and now wash his head, and cauterize it with an olive cautery. And now cauterize that with a cautery of cloves with two cauteries over the two eyebrows below the hair one small.
And guard you from the artery, lest you light it.
And of the cautery of cloves this is the form.
Chapter 15.
Of cauterization of softening of eyelids of holes.
When the eyelid of the hole is softened by illness or by moisture, then cauterize that eyelid with one cautery with this lunar cautery; and this is its form.
And if you, cauterize that over the two eyebrows one small with two cauteries in all parts, and let them be elongated from the temples. And let the length of each cautery be according to the quantity of the eyebrow.
And do not press too much with your hand with the cautery, but according to the quantity that the third part of the eyelid is inflamed.
Chapter 16.
Of cauterization of the eyelid of the hole when the hair is turned to the parts inside and it pinches the hole.
When the hair of the hole is turned to the parts inside so that it pinches the hole, cauterize in those according to two methods; for cauterization there is with fire or with burning medicine.
If you cauterize it with fire, command the patient to look at his hair as they cut them so that they are elongated and singed; and if he pinches that, then you strengthen his holes with a bandage so that they are not wounded until the hair is born.
Therefore when they are born and singed, then put the head of the patient in the hand, and now sign over the eyelid of the holes of him with a tent, with a mark which is according to the figure of a dead leaf; and let the mark be near to the hair.
Then put soft bandage in alum of wool or in poultice of poppy over the hole.
And now heat the cautery, of which this is its form.
And now cauterize over the figure which you have marked, bit by bit, in few turns, until it is burned the surface of the collar bone which is as if with a leaf of myrrh, all appearing properly.
And sign of health of your work is that you see the eyelid of the hole already contracted and the hair of it elevated from the puncture of the hole.
And therefore lift up your hand and lay him for three days, and now put over him a bandage with linen until the scar is healed. And now heal that with ointment until it is healed.
But if the hair returns for any cause then let its opening and the eyelid is softened, then do another time the cauterization over that all as you did first.
But if the hair is in the eyelid below, then cauterize that until it is elevated to its natural location and singed and let not the hair pinch the hole.
The cautery with burning medicine that you command the patient to look at his hair so that they are elongated and singed; and now let it be made of linen the form of leaf of myrrh.
And now take of soap mixed with honey and of oil of castor bean one unc. .I. Take that, and now mix those causes together, and do that with fomentation so that it is not cold; and now spread of that over the linen which is made thus with the form of leaf of myrrh, and put that over one hole or both; and put under the hole a soft bandage in alum of wool, and let the head of the patient be in its hand.
And put it over the medicine and press that one bit and not wound him until the patient feels the bite of the medicine, for bite is in it as if with fire.
And therefore when you perceive that the hole is bitten, then look at the medicine and take it away with your hand; therefore when the bite ceases, then remove the medicine and wash the hole with water; and now consider if he sees the eyelid already lifted as it is washed after constriction with fire or with incision, for then let it be; and if he returns to that of the medicine over the location in which the medicine has not acted and not become black until its action is done and is contracted.
And now put over it a bandage with linen until the collar bone of the constriction is healed, and now heal that with ointment dafinicon or other until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you, in your operation, to guard with diligent vigilance that nothing of the medicine falls into the eye, and if the eyelid becomes swollen after a few days due to some injury from hair in the eye, then apply your medicine again to the place where the eyelid is swollen, and proceed exactly as you did at the beginning, and gradually improve until it is healed.
And this is the form of the myrrh poultice.
And know that men's eyes are diverse according to their size and smallness, and therefore your incision should be made accordingly.
And do not hide the path of rectitude from him who is being taught this art.
Chapter .xvii.
Of cauterization for a fistula that is in the tear duct of the eye.
When you are treating a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases and do not perform your cure, then know that you should cauterize it according to this manner: order the patient to rest his head in your lap, and have someone else hold his head steady with their hands so that his head is neither moved nor shaken.
Then place a piece of cotton wool soaked in honey or in the mucilage of psyllium over the patient's eye.
And heat the cautery, of which this is the form:
which should be hollow, thus in the shape of a cane or of an owl' s feather, from one end of which the cautery is made.
And if you wish, it may be solid all the way through to the other end. And if you want it to be hollow inside, then make it thus with an opening.
However, what is hollow is better for your work.
And press the fistula if it is open, and draw out from it pus and fluid to dry up that place. And if it is not open, then open it and extract the matter from it.
And then place the cautery which should be well ignited, and hold your hand close to the cautery near the nose, so that your hand does not shake or the patient be disturbed, and then apply the cautery to the margin of the eye and corrupt it there.
And so if at the beginning of your cautery it penetrates into the bone, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice if necessary, and leave it thus for three days, and then place over that place cotton wool and wrap it up with a bandage until it is healed.
But if eleven days have passed and it is not healed, then apply to it a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed and scrape it according to what is appropriate in that chapter.
And there is another manner of cautery for a fistula which some first mentioned: enter the fistula and open it up, and then place in that fissure fine lead subtilely formed thus: melt the lead and pour it into the eye; hold your hand steady with good retention so that the patient is not disturbed by the molten lead entering the eye, and see to it that you apply over the eye cotton wool soaked in honey or water, for the lead adheres to the place of the fistula and heals it by a marvelously wonderful cure.
And if the fistula is healed with what we have said about the cautery and the cure, that is good; and if not, then it is necessary to administer a cut to the nose and reduce the fistula into the cavity of the nose according to its proper location.

Chapter .xix.
Of cauterization for a fistula in the mouth.
When in the root of the uvula or in the palate or in the roots of the teeth there is a boil and it has burst, and it is aged, and suppurates and there is a fistula, and you cure it and your cure is not effective, then know that you should ignite the cautery according to the amount received in the fistula, and then place the iron hot into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the hot iron penetrates the root of it; do this once or twice, and cure it with what we have said about the cure until it is healed.
And so if the pus is discharged and it is healed, that is good; and if not, then it is necessary to expose the location and scrape away the corrupted bone according to what comes in that chapter.
Chapter .xx.
Of cauterization of teeth and of softening of gums.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are shaken, and you cure them with medicines and your cure is not effective, then order the patient to rest his head in your lap, and heat the cautery, of which the form will come immediately below, so that you place the cotton wool over the tooth and push into it the hot cautery quickly, and hold your hand close so that the patient feels the heat of the fire at the root of the tooth from which it came.
And then raise your hand, and repeat the cautery several times according to what you wish.
And then let the patient rinse his mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour, and then spit it out, because the shaken tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is hardened, and the corrupted moisture is dried up.
Chapter .xxi.
Of cauterization for toothache.
When toothache is caused by coldness, or it is cold or red, or the cure with medicine is not effective, then the cautery is in two ways: with a cow' s lard, or with fire.
The cautery with lard is that you take lard of cows and melt it in the hollow of iron, and then take cotton wool and wrap it around the end of the tooth, and then dip that in the hot lard and place it on the painful tooth until it is numbed.
And then repeat that several times until the power of the fire penetrates to the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, dip wool or cotton in the lard and place it on the painful tooth, and hold over that hot iron until the iron penetrates the cavity of the tooth.
However, the cautery with fire is that you take an iron or needle and heat it in the fire until it is red hot, and there is no thickness in it and the keenness of the fire does not penetrate the mouth of the patient.
Then heat the cautery thus, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand so that the cautery is numbing; do this several times because the pain will be reduced or in that day or the next day.
And know that by pressure of that cautery that the patient fills his mouth with good breath and holds it for an hour, and then spits it out; this is the manner of the cautery.
And cauterize it as much as you can.
And this is the shape of the tube:
Chapter .XXII.
Of cauterization of hernia.

And if the hernia is small, then apply the cautery according to the amount of the hernia, and let it sit for three days, and place a bandage soaked in hot water over it while it is still warm from the fire.
And then cure that with ointment, poultices and linen until it is healed.

Chapter .XXVII.

Chapter 30.
On cauterization of meles.
When you cure the illness of a mele with what we have said about curing it in the division, and don't trust your treatment, then cauterize it according to three methods, all of which are correct; the first is that you make three or four cauteries that are parallel to the length of the mele according to the figure of the cauteries of the heart, the figure of which has preceded.
And between each cautery let there be the thickness of a finger or a little more, and the manner of the cautery should be as we have said about the cautery of the heart in the same way.
And don't press your hand down on the cautery, and let the patient lie on his back.
And another way to cauterize is that you ignite the cautery while holding two windings, and this cause we have said in the chapter on dislocation of the muscle; and raise up the pustule which is in the bend of the mele where the patient's left hand lies.
And let your elevation by which you raise up the pustule be according to the length of the body, so that the cauteries are made according to the width of the body.
And then intertwine the two windings and ignite them while pushing into the pustule from the other side as well.
And then pull out the cautery; and so there are four cauteries made.
And if you want, cauterize with a cautery having three windings.
And then you cure the cautery after it has stopped giving out pus for many days because only then are the other causes that precede in the cure effective.
Chapter 31.

And the quantity of the depth of the cautery should be proportional to the thickness of the pustule.
And then pull out the cautery after it has been in for a long time.
And don't evacuate the patient from the cure after the cautery so that two intentions are added to it and healing is accelerated for him by aid.
The form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be key-shaped according to what is above it, and that with which the back is cauterized is olive-shaped according to what precedes it.

Chapter 7.
Of the treatment of pain in the ears.
Many times some children suck from their mothers' bellies and do not pierce them, and this happens in some men as well, with pain in the middle of the ear due to cold or due to a wound in that part; and this pain is sometimes caused by an obstacle in the hole of the ear, and sometimes it is in the outer parts.
And that which happens in the middle, which does not affect the membrane, is in the more difficult dispositions to heal.
And when you have achieved the membrane, see that you hold the ear towards the sun and examine it. And so if you see obvious swelling, open it with a thin spatula of which this is the shape:
If its end is narrow where the width is small, and one side is pointed and the other is not; and the spatula should be of two edges so that it does not injure the ear.
And if the pain is due to a wound born in the ear or in its middle, then open it with fine pincers and cut it fiercely until it is entirely exposed.
And if the pain is in the hole of the ear, then take a thin rod and heat it in the fire for a little, and then insert it into the middle of the ear.
And so if you have felt swelling with ease due to an obstruction, release the pressure of it with ease; and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear.
And then place over the ear a bandage according to the amount of the width of the wound which you have wrapped around it; and do this for several days until you are certain of the healing of the wound; or take some cotton wool and soak it in vinegar and powder it with ground pepper and use it; and if you see that the ear is already swollen, then remove the cotton wool and replace it with another one which you have soaked in rose oil, until the ulcerated part has healed; and then treat it until it is well.
If there is bleeding, then soak a sponge or cloth in water and place it on the wound, and use the other treatment which restricts the flow of blood, which is described in the treatise on distillation.
Chapter VIII.
On the treatment of Athaizeel, which extends to the eyelids.
Athaizeel, which affects the eyelids of some people with moisture, and others with dryness.
Therefore, if you have them, take the am tenhalhas or am onci, and cut off their branches from the roots, and place it over the affected areas after crushing it.
But if there is pain with bleeding, then you should cauterize it with a very thin anticular cautery.
And the best cauterization is to cut and pull them out from their roots, and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
Chapter IX.
On the treatment of grandeyssa that affects the eyelids of men.
In many cases it occurs in the eyelids of men for some reason which is similar to grandissia in its strength and hardness, and because of this it is called grandeyssa.
And it is an accumulation of thick humidity under and above the eyelid.
Therefore, the treatment for them is that one should consider whether the grandissia is proceeding from something appearing on the eyelid and spread all over it; and the cause of this is leukemia.
Therefore, cut a slit in it according to its width, and then dig out all of it with ease so that it comes out, and then suspend it with am onci and cut it off.
And if the wound is large, then you should sew it up; and treat it until it is healed.
And if it is small, you will not suffer from it because the eye restores it and the flesh grows back.
And if the grandissia is declining towards the inner parts of the eyelid, then cut off the surface within it, and then suspend the grandissia with am onci, another that you should dig out from its roots, and press it from all sides, and if the eyelid is cut open because of this, then it does not matter.
And after the incision, wash the eye with salted water; and treat the wound so that it heals.
Chapter X.
On the treatment of axcirnah above the eyelid.
Axcirnah is a disease which affects the membranes of the upper eyelid, and mostly affects children, harming those whose eyes it occurs in, causing them to close their eyes because of it.
And because of this, you will see them all the time on their faces, and they sleep with their eyes closed; and the eyelids below are wet, covered in inflammation, and an apparent protuberance is visible on their eyes; and when you press it with your fingers, you feel it inside.
And one way of treating it is for the patient to place his head in your lap, and then place a cloth on him and make him take a cold bath, and make a circle according to the amount which contains arthernach all around, and then place it over the affected area and press it with your fingers from all sides so that it becomes attached; and then cut out the middle of that humidity with a pointed instrument making an incision according to its width, and the incision should not be larger than the one made in flaubotomia.
But in the case where you split the cord all the way so that it reaches the arcernach, for in most cases the arcernach comes about through an incision according to the shape of white grayness.
Therefore, extract it with cloths which you have wrapped between your fingers on the outside and twisted between the right and left hand so that it is dispersed.
And be careful not to push into the incision with the instrument so that you do not reach the eye and loosen it.
But if you do not see arternach at the beginning of the incision, but you push into the incision with ease so that it occurs; and then extract it as we have said before; and then soak the cloths in water and wine and place them over the affected area and press them hard.
And so that it is crushed with salt and placed over the cavity of the incision so that what remains of that humidity is removed.
And then treat it until it is healed.
But if an abscess occurs on the wound, then treat it with mild poultices until it is healed.

Chapter .xii.
Of the elevation of poking hairs in the eye with a needle when the hair is hard.
When there are unnatural, hard, rough and poking hairs in the eye, then the operation in this case is that you take a thin needle and insert it into that delicate thread of cedar and lion, and then tie the extremes of it in a very subtle manner. And let the length of the threads be the quantity of a palm.
And then you tie another subtle thread underneath it briefly, and knot the extremes of that if you want to.
And then place the patient’s head in your lap, and be near the window so that your work is revealed, for it is a subtle and minute operation.
And then insert the needle into the root of the hair which has the need for ingenuity, and make that penetrate the eyelid quickly while you extract that one above the natural hair.
And then pull the hair inside out and insert it into the eye, and let there be one or two or three hairs and not more.
And then pull your hand with that one so that the hair is pulled out with the eye with the natural hair.
But if it is pulled out inside-out and the hair is not extracted, you will pull out the inside-out one to the sides with the thread which you have tied around that one, so that it is extracted from the eyebrow above.
And you will wash that one with the vision of the eye, for then you will pull out the inside-out one and the thread, and let each one and close the eye, and leave the bandage for two or three days, so that the hair adheres to its place and grows on good flesh.
And if the hair is longer, then you tie a long one of the natural hairs, and it is elevated with that one, or let the one you have inserted be elevated in order to lengthen it, and then you elevate that one.
Chapter .xiii.
Of the cure of the ulcer which comes in the eyelid above.
When there is an ulcer in the eyelid, and it is contraction of the eyelid when it is contracted on one side or the other, from poor healing of the wound or from incision or cautery, and it is called leporina, and this ulceration or is natural or accidental, and it is done by healing of the wound or from incisions or cautery, or by similarity to them badly-cured.
The manner of the operation in this case is that you split that healing and separate its lips, and place it in what is between those one fold of linen thread, and tie those ones so they are healed.
And do not use curing of it from the causes which dry out and constrict; for if you do that, return to ulceration worse than never before.
Use on that which softens as it is fenugreek, and moisten with the water in which are soaked fennel and aniseed, or anoint with oil of myrrh, and submerge that one in the bandage, and heal with that.
And the chief point of your cure is that you pierce with all ingenuity which is not healed according to the form it was at the beginning.
And this operation which we have said is not but some rectification of ulceration that does not return the shape of the place according to what it was before.

This ulceration which is done in the eyelid below, which is aptly named ulceration; and it is of one natural, another accidental.

Chapter 19.
Of the reduction of hernia in the nose.

And this should be done several times, and then restore the place with drying and astringent causes.

Chapter 20.
Of the reduction of the eminence of a wound.
When the wound protrudes in its entirety and no harm or diminution happens in the bleeding, then you should lax the patient, and then you should hold him by the neck and suck out with good suction; and then place ventouse on the neck with scarification and sucking with strong suction; and then place liniment which is made of copper scale and aloe and myrrh, and then tighten the dressing over the wound with fine powders.

And then place those one over the other according to the quantity of which the wound has need. And then tighten over that with a hard cloth with strong compression; and repeat the ventouses with suction without scarification; and then stop the ventouses and let the wound rest day and night.
But if in between the ligament is softened, then you should be made to be tight.
And then stop the ligament then day and night as we have said.
And if you see the wound already reduced, well and good, and if not, then repeat the dressing with the powders and the compression and the ventouses until it is healed.

Chapter .XXIV.
Of the cure of swollen nose.
