But if the humidity does not penetrate according to that which is covered, then you know that inside it is swollen meat in the bones of the nose from which no incision has been made.
Then you see if in the one which there is any thickness, and nipple on it with fingers, and place between each nail the quantity of the finger or less, and push into the nose and enter an extremity of the needle in the nose for the ray or another cause by which it is possible to it.
And after that is done, let him breathe in so that it goes into the channels of the nose, and he breathes out over his throat, for troops look like this action do children in schools, and is a distant cause to that which wants to be done.
Then tie the two ends of the gallbladder, one end coming out over the nose and the other going into the nose, and administer a cauterization of flesh with the nails that are in the gallbladder, and do this until you know that the flesh is cauterized at the nails of the gallbladder.
Then extract the gallbladder and in the nose apply an abstraction of blood with a cautery, and do this for three days or more until the cautery has corroded all that is rotten in the flesh.
And at the end of the cause, insert a lead cane into the nose for several days until it is healed.
But if you have a more effective cure, use that instead.
And this is the form of the instrument for an emetic that draws oils and medicines into the nose:
And do this with silver or brass, which should be similar to a small lamp, also with a small cavity and the spout similarly.
And if you want, make a closed tube like a cane, and the spout of the emetic instrument should be flat and uncovered; it should have a handle at its rear end, with which you can draw oils or waters that you want from suckable fluids and causes.
Chapter 25.
Of wounds in the ends of the nose.
Many times a wound occurs in the ends of the nose, and it increases and swells for several days until something is put on it to heal it.
And by that time you should have applied the beginning of its appearance, and you should have removed all of that. Then apply over the site a cautery or burning medicine which is in the location of the wound.
But if its beginning is delayed until it has become magnified, then consider whether it is suppurating, hard, of dusky color and of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron, for this suppuration often brings great harm to the person upon whom you are doing it.
And if the suppuration is of a painful nature and not of dusky color, and its beginning is possible in everything, then evacuate the patient and do it without fear, and treat the site with something that dries and constricts until it is healed.
Chapter 26.
Of the sewing of the nose and of the lips and of the ear when the continuity is dissolved by pus or by similar things.
Know that when a solution of continuity occurs in one of these cartilages, few confer about this operation except in some men.
Therefore, when for some cause of those you consider that it is fresh pus with its blood, then join the two lips of the pus with a suture, and then cure that until it is healed.
And if the lips of the solution of continuity are already separated and each one is made healthy, then cut each party of the visible tendon within which the blood flows. Then join the two lips with a suture and strengthen those, and over them pulverize dragon's blood and pounded vinegar, and place over the powder a pad of diaphoretic plaster, or one of the other plasters of consolida tion, and let that lie for two or three days, and then remove that plaster and change that plaster, and let it lie until the wounds by themselves are healed.
But the manner of the suture is that you add the solution of continuity or with needles as we have mentioned in the suture of the belly, or add the solution of continuity with gallbladder as we have made known to you.
Chapter 27.
Of the extraction of those causes that come in the two lips in the divided parts within.
Many times in many men in the divided parts of their lips there are some suppurations hard and resembling grass, and some of them are minor and some are major.
Therefore you should convert the lips and cut each one of those hardnesses throughout its whole part, and then fill up the incision with powdered sage within so that the blood is constricted, and then wash it with vinegar and cure the site with something that is astringent until it is healed.
Chapter 28.
Of incision of the flesh joined in the gums.
Many times there is upon the gum joined flesh which the ancients called albus, therefore you should suspend that with an ointment or have that with forceps and cut that after its root, and let the pus run or the blood.
Then apply over the site powdered sage or other styptic or astringent powders.
And if that flesh returns, then cut it secondarily, and cauterize it, for by cauterizing it will not return.
Chapter 29.
Of extraction of teeth with iron.
When upon the surface of the teeth in the divided parts within and between the gums are joined rough, sharp, and some times black escorsions and the teeth are made green or yellow, and within the gum is seen corruption and the teeth are made black.
Therefore you should make the patient open his mouth between his hands and push down his head toward his chest, and cut the teeth in which those escorsions appear and the causes seem like sand so that no cause remains within, and do this of the blackness and of the yellowing and of the others until they are cleansed.
Therefore if that which is in the beginning of the root is rotten, well then; but if not, then you should repeat the incision over those another day and the second and the third until it comes to its final state in whatever you want.
And know that teeth have need of many different knives with diverse shapes and figures according to the preparation for your operation. And therefore the knife with which the tooth is cut from the divided part within is another than the knife with which it is cut between the teeth according to other forms, and these forms of knives should be prepared by you as follows:
Chapter 30.
Of uprooting teeth.
Let the tooth be cured from its pain by all means and delayed in every uprooting of it, for there is no cause that supplants its existence when it has been uprooted, for it is a sublime substance within which is an excuse in its uprooting.
But when the patient is forced to have that tooth uprooted, you should certifiably know which is the painful tooth, for many times the pain deceives the patient and seems to be in a healthy tooth and you uproot it and then the pain does not cease until the painful and sick tooth is uprooted, for we have seen this through operation of the barbits.
Therefore when you are certified which is the painful tooth and know it well, then cut in the circuit of the tooth with a spatula in which there is some verticity, so that it is dissolved from the gum throughout its whole division, and then maul it with your fingers or with slender forceps little by little within until you have reached it.
And then pull out the teeth with force using a strong plier or instrument, and place the patient's head between your thighs so that he does not bite you, and then treat the tooth according to its position so that you do not break it or cause the patient greater pain.
And if it is not dislocated, then take one of those instruments and put it under the tooth from all sides with ease and force its removal so that it is done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is broken or worn down, then you must cover that break with a piece of cloth and grip it tightly at its base with tweezers so that it does not break when you are tightening it with pliers.
And you must open it carefully with an incision all around the gum and be very careful not to break it or tear it apart, and return to the patient so that he suffers less pain than before.
And be sure not to do what some ignorant barber-surgeons do in their foolhardiness and audacity during tooth extractions; for they do not administer what we have recommended, and many times they bring on great diseases in men which are more difficult to cure than before, and the roots of their teeth remain whole or partly intact, or they extract them with some bones of the jaw as we have often witnessed.
And then after the extraction let the mouth be washed with warm wine or vinegar and salt.
And if it bleeds profusely as it often does, then mix some powder of alum and sprinkle it on the wound; and if that alum does not stop the bleeding, cauterize it.
The shape of the pliers and tweezers with which you pull out the tooth at first should have a long shank, a short handle, and be thick so that they do not bend when you use them to work.
And let their shanks be as short as possible so that when you grip with them they do not bend; let their shanks be short.
And let them be made of Indian iron with straight shanks and let the shanks have teeth that mesh together and grip tightly; some of their shanks are shaped like a stork's beak, which is hooked, and they grip very tightly.
Chapter 31.
On the extraction of teeth and the breaking of the jaw bones.
When you must extract a tooth that is broken, then you should put on the site a poultice for one or two days until the site is softened; and then insert a forceps or pliers whose ends are shaped like a stork's beak or hooked, the shape of the pliers:
Their ends should be serrated like a file or chisel.
And if you do not obey my instructions with these forceps or pliers, then you should cut into the gum and expose all the flesh, and insert the instrument called an awl, which is a small lever whose shape is like this:
And let it be short with a thick shank, and not bent so that it does not break.
Then if by doing this the root is exposed, well and good; but if not, help yourself with these other instruments of which these are the shapes: the shape of the first instrument is triangular at its shank end in which there should be some thickness:
The shape of the second instrument is that it should have a triangular and more slender end.
And now help yourself with this instrument which has two ramps whose shape is as follows: and with other instruments which are used in tooth extractions; for the aid is made with this instrument which is shaped like a large needle, and this is its shape:
The triangular end should be curved or cut short and have some thickness; let it not be bent so that it does not break.
And another variation on the instruments for teeth is to make them similarly to the others.
But the clever and skilled practitioner in this art finds for himself methods according to what his experience and diverse illnesses teach him; for there are illnesses to which the ancients did not attribute or assign proper instruments because of their various shapes.
But if the jaw bone or any other bone is broken, or if there is pus, then let it be treated at that site with what is appropriate from the instruments and pliers we have mentioned in the extraction of tooth roots; and help yourself with an instrument whose shape is like this:
And let there be some thickness added to it little by little, and let it be bound or held in place by the mouth so that it does not slip or leak until the bone is healed; and then dress the wound with appropriate remedies for that.
But if there is a small ulcer in the bone, then scrape away that ulcer and its blackness, and treat it until it is healed.
Chapter 32.
On the treatment of prominent teeth above the others.
When teeth are prominent not according to their natural form because of their shape, and especially when this occurs in women, and especially in old women, then consider: if the tooth is attached to another tooth, and there is no space or room for it, then pull it out; but if it is not attached to another tooth, then you cut it down with that instrument whose shape is like this; and it is similar to a pig's tusk, and it should be made of Indian iron with a very sharp end.
And make your incision in it which you will use to cut into it in several places because of the hardness of the tooth, and that it does not affect any other teeth.
And if the prominent tooth is expanded with file, then file it with an Indian iron file whose shape is like this:
And let it be all of Indian iron and very sharp; and let it have many small points like a file with which the tooth is filed little by little in several places with ease, so that no other tooth is affected and it does not break. And then line that up in its width, and cut that away with some razors.
And if that tooth whose part is broken and touches the tongue, then let you file it down until the sharp edge of that fracture is filed down and smoothed, and let it be flattened so that the tongue is not cut or speech impaired.
Chapter 33.
On the restoration of broken teeth with gold or silver wire.
When the teeth have received a concussion and removal due to impact or biting, and the patient cannot chew on it, and you have treated that with astringent remedies, and your treatment has not worked, then so that they do not become loose as they are bound with gold wire and not with silver wire, for silver becomes blackened but gold does not; and let them be bound, and after several days, but gold will not darken.
And let the wire be of such thickness and coarseness according to the amount that can fit between the teeth; and the shape of the twist is that you take the wire and wind it twice around two healthy teeth, and then let it grow with two twists of the wire between two broken teeth, or if one or more, in such a way that the thread comes to the healthy tooth from the other broken tooth. And then repeat the massage in the area where you started, strengthening your hand with skill and wisdom so that there is no discomfort.
And tighten the string with which you draw the teeth roots so that it does not leak.
Then cut the ends of the superfluous thread with forceps or tweezers, and place them in each spot with gestures, and turn them and hide them between the healthy tooth and the damaged tooth so that it does not cause harm to the tongue. Then let that remain tight like a Roman bow.
But if it is loose or torn, strengthen it or them with another thread in the same way at all times.
And this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the direction of two healthy teeth and two damaged ones, thus with their threads tied:
And when one or two teeth are pushed back into their sockets and have grown back as we have described, and they hurt again:
And it does not happen unless by a skilled and wise artist.
And sometimes it is necessary to use a bone from a cow, and it is shaped like a tooth, and placed in the place where the tooth is lacking, and strengthened as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
Chapter .xxxiv.
Of the beginning of the swelling that comes in the tongue, and prohibits speech.
This ligament which comes below the tongue sometimes happens naturally or accidentally as a result of a plague which is already consolidated.
And the operation in it is that you open the mouth of the patient, his head being in your lap; and raise his tongue, and then cut that nervous ligament according to the width by which the tongue is released from its bondage.
But if there is any hardness or knotting in it, and it has become so because of the consolidation of plague, then you apply an unguent and cut it where you cut the ligament and the knot is dissolved.
And beware that there be no fissure in the membrane of the flesh, and that you cut through here with an incision and blood flows out.
Then wash the trace of the incision with wine vinegar or with pure wine, or with water mixed with vinegar; and then place a cotton swab under the tongue, or a bandage which the patient keeps under his tongue every night so that nothing else is consolidated there.
But if blood flows out, place a mixture of vitriol over the spot; but if pus flows out, then cauterize the spot with a red-hot cautery which is appropriate for that. And then let it be cured by the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter .xxxv.
Of the extraction of a ranula under the tongue.
Sometimes it happens under the tongue an abscess resembling a small lump, which prohibits the tongue from performing its natural functions, and when it is enlarged it fills the mouth.
And the operation in this case is that you open the mouth of the patient facing the sun and examine the abscess.
And if you see it dark or black in color, hard to which the patient does not respond with feeling, then do not touch that because it is rotten.
And if it is inclined towards whiteness, and there is moisture in which there is humidity, then you put an unguent on it, and cut it with a sharp blade, and cut it throughout its entire length; and if blood flows out during your operation, then you place over it a mixture of vitriol so that the blood is restrained.
Then return to your work until you have finished it, after which wash it with wine vinegar and salt, and let it be cured by the other cure for that until it is healed.
Chapter .xxxvi.
Of the extraction of an abscess from two ears and of that which is found in the gullet, and of the other abscesses.
When you find in the gullet a swelling which is like glands which are similar to cotton, and they are discharged from the outside and are called two ears, and when you cure them with what we have said in the division and it is not healed, then consider if the abscess is hard, of dark color, of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron.
And if it is of a red color and the root is thick, then do not touch that with iron for the flow of blood; before you remove it let that mature, and then either you will draw out that or it will burst by itself.
And if it is of a white color, soft, and the root of it is fine, then that is what should be cut.
And the operation in this case is that you consider before your operation whether the abscess has rested after being cauterized completely or if it has diminished by any lessening; and then cause the patient to sit facing the sun, and his head be in your lap, and open his mouth, and the assistant holding with his hand press down the tongue of the patient from above with a noble instrument, of which this is the form:
And let it be made of silver or of copper, and let it be fine like a needle.
Then when you press down with that the tongue and it is shown to you the abscess, and put over that your iron weight, then take unguent and smear that on the root of it, and draw out that to the outer parts as much as you can. Another thing which you draw some cause from the membranes, and then cut that with an instrument of which this is the form:
Another thing which you draw some cause from the membranes, and then cut that with an instrument of which this is the form: It is like forceps except the ends of it are curved so that the orifice of each of them is in the direction of the other, being sharp, let that be made of iron hardened in vinegar.
But if that instrument is not at hand, then cut that with a blade of which this is the form: And let it be sharp on one side, blunt on the other side.
And after you have cut one wound, cut the other according to this way of cutting, and then wash the wound of the patient with water mixed with vinegar.
But if blood flows out, then wash it with water of a decoction of bark of a pomegranate or of bayberry leaves and like that of the causes of stipting within so that the flow of blood is restrained, and then let it be cured by that until it is healed.
And sometimes it happens in the gullet other abscesses, and those two ears as well; and cut those according to what we have said in the cutting of two wounds equally.
And there was a woman who had an abscess which was found in the gullet of her, that abscess tended towards a dark color, with little feeling, and it had closed the gullet of her, and the woman breathed with difficulty, and already prohibited from eating and drinking water, and she was already nearing death if she did not last for one day or two.
And the abscess had swollen so that it had formed two bumps within which poured out through two holes.
Then she cut it with a sharp blade and inserted one of the tips into that abscess, and drew out that, and tied up is from her mouth a great portion, and then she cut the other wound as we have said before, and then she closed his mouth, and pressed down his tongue, and then she smeared the unguent on that abscess.
And then she cut a great portion from it, and there flowed out from it only a little blood. Then the bleeding of that woman stopped, and she immediately began to drink water and eat food; therefore I did not cease cutting out that boil several times over a long time, and then the boil appeared in another place where it was cut out, as it was growing.
Then I bandaged and cauterized his boil, therefore on the next day; and then I walked around and did not know what God had done to him.
Chapter 37.
On cutting out a boil when it is suppurating.
When pus comes out of the boil and it is suppurating and long, then it is called a furuncle; and if it is at the top thick and round, then it is called a bubo.
But if it is healed with the water that we have mentioned in the previous chapter and does not respond to your treatment, and you see that suppuration continues, then be careful about cutting it, for there is danger to the patient when suppuration continues.
And when you see it according to what I have said about its whiteness and length, then make the patient fast and press his tongue with an instrument of which process has been mentioned in the incision of two teeth, and stick it into the gum and cut that with one of the two instruments of which are spoken in the incision of two teeth.
And you must not cut it unless it is above its natural limit; for if you cut more, you will hurt his jaw.
And after the incision, use what we have recommended in the incision of two teeth, and heal it until it is cured.
But if the patient is afraid of having his jaw cut, then use the cauterization without fear, and the manner of the cauterization in it is only with acute water; and you must place the head of the patient in your lap, and press his tongue with the instrument we have mentioned, and take the water we have spoken of in the chapter on cauterization, and do this with a live coal, and pour that not thick nor subtle into the cavity of the instrument of which this is the form:
Let the end of it be hollow like a spoon, in which the medicine is put as in a spoon; and place the instrument with the medicine on the boil, and let the patient lean over on his side so that saliva or mucous from the mouth does not fall back into the wound.
And with your hand hold the medicine and press it onto the uvula through the space of about a half-hour until you see it blackened and subdued by the biting of the medicine.
And if you want, take a piece of cloth and wrap it around the end of the jaw, and submerge the cloth in the medicine, and insert the jaw with the cloth into a tube as far as the jaw adheres to that tube, and do this several times until you achieve what you want from the cauterization of the uvula; then let it be for three or four days.
And if you find that the medicine needs to be repeated, then repeat it; and after the cauterization, cleanse around the uvula with a cloth dipped in water, and cleanse what is inside the mouth of the medicine, and let it be washed with soapwater, and let it be healed outside with ointment, and inside with gargles until it is cured.
And this kind of cure is more safe than incision, and less painful from fear.
Sometimes the uvula is healed in a way that is more subtle than cauterization and incision: take gallnuts, hyssop, oregano, ruda, scilla, arabic alkanet, camomile, bromine and other herbs like them, and mix all those ingredients, or some of them, into a cake; and let the cake be cooked in a decent pot, and let there be a hole in the middle of the cake, on which is placed an instrument made of silver or iron.
And let the end be inserted into the mouth of the patient so that the steam reaches the uvula over the glottis, until the uvula becomes very foggy.
And after that repeat on it several times until it is dried up; and beware of doing this cure during the day when there is a suppuration of boils, for then it would be too much on the boil; so you must not do this.
But if you do not have this instrument, then take a reed and tie on the end of it a cloth of hemp, so that the mouth of the patient is burned, for the cloth of hemp prohibits the steam from burning the mouth.
And this cure is good for health.
Chapter 38.
On the extraction of thorns and of what adheres in the throat and from other causes.
Sometimes there is adhesion in the throat, or thorn of a stone or some other cause.
Then you must extract what is evident from those, on which the eye falls, when you press the tongue with an instrument in front of the sun, so that it is revealed to you what is in the throat.
And what is not apparent and hidden in the throat, then you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach, for it is certain that the cause of the throat is brought up by vomiting; or that the patient licks a piece of soapwort or a leaf of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread; or that he takes a piece of dried sea sponge and chews it hard with his teeth, and then makes him vomit so that what is in the throat is extracted. And if he takes a piece of eel and chews it, and then vomits it out, or takes an onion and chews it and vomits it out, then it is extracted.
But if it is not extracted with the causes we have mentioned, then use an instrument made of lead in this form:
Let it be thicker than a little finger, and let the end of it be hollow which you insert into his throat with ease.
And let him raise his head up, and beware of the touching of his bones in the throat, so that it does not push it into his throat, or that he touch with his hand.
But let him insert that end gently into his throat with his knowledge of the location of the cause and push it inwards, and pull out his hand with the instrument upwards, as far as it is prepared to be extracted.
Chapter 39.
On the extraction of blood-spitting annexed to the throat.
When blood-spitting is cured with what we have mentioned in the division of the cure with medicines and does not respond, then consider after that in the throat of the patient towards the sun, for you will see that his tongue is swollen with the instrument which I have recommended.
Then if you see the blood-spitting, extract it with a small needle or with decently subtle instruments.
And if you are not able to extract it with that, then take a hollow tube and insert it into the throat of the patient, and after that place in the cavity of the tube an iron needle which has been heated, and do this several times (until the blood-spitting is stopped and comes out of the throat) and let the patient abstain from water for all the day.
And then take a washcloth soaked in warm water, open their mouth with it, and wash their mouth with it; and do not give them anything to drink for one hour or so with your hand, for the blood will flow immediately when they feel the water.
But if it is not cured with what we have recommended, then smoke the patient with camphor or assafetida using the instrument which we have recommended for smoking the uvula.
Do this, depending on how far gone they are.
And there is another way of operating on this: that you take a vessel in which are burning coals and the vessel be covered with a covering in the middle of which there is a hole; and the end of the instrument be placed in that hole; and then let the smoking take place; and let the patient place their mouth at the end of the tube, and close their mouth so that the smoking is not wasted until you know that the smoking has reached the blood, for then the blood will flow immediately.
And if it does not work, then repeat the smoking several times, and keep the patient from drinking, and let him eat salty foods and lard, and do not give them water, and thus it is necessary that this regimen be followed.
And this is the form of the instrument with which blood is drawn from the gullet when it is seen; and it is like tweezers, except that there is some curvature in it. And it is placed at the gullet, and its end is similar to a stork's beak, which is gloved, in which there is tightened with a thread, so that when we press any spot, it does not leak.
Chapter 40.
In which is the sum of the discussion on ulcers and their treatment.
Ulcers are of many kinds, according to what is remembered of them in this book.
And they are diverse in their penetration and section by two methods: one is by the kind of ulcer within themselves; and the other is according to what we know of their moisture.
And the second method is according to the locations in the body where they occur, for the ulcer that occurs on the head is different from the one that occurs on the tail; and the ulcer on the fleshy location is different from the one that occurs at a joint; and each of them has its own treatment by operation.
And there are some ulcers which do not penetrate but rather mature the pus within them, or else they are fulfilled in themselves.
And there are other ulcers which are not cut open unless their pus matures within them and they are fulfilled: these are the ulcers near the joints; for when an ulcer comes near a joint, its nature is prolonged through that which it affects of its parts, and corrupts the tendons or nerves of that joint, so that it causes contraction in that member, or else it affects the main member, and if you delay piercing it, it matures in the main member; or it is near the tail, therefore do not pierce it unless it is matured, lest it corrupt the parts within the tail, or unless it is made in the end of it so that it does not corrupt the parts within the tail and is prolonged to the parts within the tail, and a fistula be formed, or that it be made in its term so that it may not be healed. But know the time of piercing the ulcer, and then it is when it has matured.
And know that it has matured when there is a decrease in pain and fever, and also the lessening of heat and pulse, and the sharpening of the tip of the ulcer, and the other signs.
And know that piercing occurs at the bottom of the pus-filled location of the ulcer and from the pus coming out of the eminence of its cure.
And piercing should always be according to the length of the flesh or body, if the ulcers are on the ends of the hands or feet, and in the places of the tendons, of the strings of the nerves, of the bowstrings; and finally, in all similar locations in which there is no reflection: for in those where there is a reflection, use piercing according to that member.
But when the ulcer is in a fleshy location, it is better to delay piercing it until its digestion is confirmed according to its fulfillment, as we have said; for if you pierce it before that, the body of the pus within it will be prolonged and there will be much corruption, and often its lips are hardened and its depth increased.
But some ulcers are pierced according to the breadth of the flesh or body, or according to which member is in need.
And you should administer small piercing in small ulcers, and in large ulcers great piercing and wide or many piercings according to the difference in the size of the ulcers.
And there are those in which the vein is hollowed out and has been cut, when it is done so that bread is made, and it is made in a term so that it may not be healed, just as that which occurs in pustules and blisters.
And there are those in which it is cut with three angles; and there is that in which it is cut like the leaf of the myrrh tree, just as in the ulcers of the armpits.
And there are those in which round section and moon-like section are administered to them, and they are similar to each other.
But that one to which there is no head as in superficial ulcers, you should pierce it with superficial piercing or flat piercing only.
And when the ulcer is large and has collected much pus, pierce it and do not be afraid to draw out all the pus in that hour; take some from it at one time, and then close up the ulcer for another day, and then take more at a greater time, and do this repeatedly until it is healed.
And especially if the patient is of a cold nature, or a woman in labor, or a small child, or an old person in decline, for the animal spirit is often resolved by the discharge of pus, and often the patient dies, and you should operate on them.
Keep this chapter with great caution, and then with your piercing by which you pierce these ulcers, wash the sloughs and consider therefore whether the slough of the ulcer is small or it is a flat section, then administer the oils of lard or of rose; and if the ulcer is large and its fissures are many, then pause the nail in each crack so that they may be filled.
And if in the ulcer a part of the vein is cut or it is hollowed out within its circuit, then you should complete it with lard fat or cloth made from linen, just as when you have drawn out pus or roots, without moisture; and strengthen that within the third day; and then process it and heal it with what you will, according to its signs.
But if there is blood flow in the hour of your operation, then administer warm water and wine mixed with a cloth made from linen, and place that on the location of the blood flow many times.
But if the blood flow persists, then you should administer regimen and cure, and apply powders which I have recommended in many places of this our book and in division.
But if it is in the winter time, and the location of the ulcer is the location of many nerves, then you should pour powders into wine and oil and place those on the locations.
And if it is summer, and the areas are fleshy, then you should apply powdered herbs mixed with water and oil or wine and oil, and let this mixture rest on the affected area for three days as we have said, and then you should open the blister and clean it and apply what is suitable for its healing.
And this is what is necessary to know about the treatment of blisters in general, but according to the method of distinction, I have already said about each type of blister and how to treat them specifically.
Chapter 41.
Of the incision of blisters which come on the nape of the neck.
On the nape of the neck, there are small blisters, and they are made up of layers of membranes which are formed; and the layers are very thin.
And from them are bumps, and from those come blisters containing humidity similar to lime. And from them are those that contain humidity resembling powder, and resembling them; and from those are the ones that are stony, hard.
And in the incision of all of them, and in the extraction of these there is no fear, as the extraction of these does not cause a pulse.

Chapter 49.
Of incisions on ulcers that occur through an artery or a vein.

Chapter 52.
Of cure of the eminence of the navel.

CHAPTER 63.

And if it is very old, its colour will be dark, and there is no heat in it.
And sometimes it is caused by a knotting of the vessels, and due to inflammation of those parts from which the testicles have already been affected, or due to inflammation of the veins.

But what is caused by inflammation of a vein will not be dispersed for any reason due to compression with the fingers.

And if there is adhesion for some reason in the flesh, or between what is between the vessels, then have all that adhesion removed and cut through it with a circular incision.
But if there is flesh growing in the place of the adhesion which is behind, then cut through all that is there and extract the water as we have said above.
Therefore when your operation is complete, then fill the wound with wool soaked in rosewater and wine; and then treat it with the other treatment until it is healed.

Chapter LXV.
On the cure of intestinal hernia.
The occurrence of this hernia is through an incision that extends inward on the abdomen from the armpits of the navel, so that loosening the intestines from that rupture enters one of the intestines.
And this rupture is either of the abdomen or from an incision in it, and these two types occur for various reasons: from a blow, or from falling, or from crying, or from lifting something heavy, or from similar causes.
And the sign of this, when it is from an extension of the abdomen, is that it occurs little by little over a long time, and does not occur suddenly, and it is an abscess swollen inside the vein because the abdomen compresses the intestine.
And the sign of this is when it is from an incision in the abdomen, because at the beginning it causes violent pain suddenly; and there is visible inflammation below the navel, and this is due to the hernia of the intestine, and the body of it at the edges outside of the abdomen.
And sometimes the intestine slips out with the membrane, and this hernia is called intestinal hernia of the scrotum.
And sometimes it is made with swelling, and sometimes there is a tear in the intestine, and here it is retained, and it is great harm to the patient, and sometimes it causes bad pain and especially when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of these species of this illness, there is fear, because one must avoid the occurrence of that.
And the manner of the operation of this is that you command the patient to reduce the intestine with his hand at the parts within his cavity if he obeys his returnment, and then he should be placed on his back between your hands, and lift his legs.

Then cut away the skin around the scrotum, so that the tough white membrane of each part is exposed.
Then you insert your finger into the opening around the testicle, where there is a tough white membrane between the scrotum and the testicle, and you cut away the membrane that attaches the second part to the back of the testicle.
Then pull the skin of the scrotum away from the testicles and towards the parts in front, and hold the tough white membrane up with your left hand, and lift the testicle up by the membrane to the part where it is cut; and tell your assistant to hold the testicle up, while you cut away the membrane behind it with a complete solution.
And make sure that there is no cause for the intestine to be wrapped around the tough white membrane. But if you find any cause in him, then you return it to his belly below.
And then pierce the part below the scrotum where blood and pus will run out, just as we have described in what we have said before.
And then apply wool soaked in oil and place it on the wound; and apply the sutures we have recommended (and sometimes the tough white membrane is cauterized where we have said to cut it, for fear of a flow of blood, which happens several times), and let the sutures fall so that they can heal by themselves.
But if its healing is delayed, then let it be soaked in hot water and place it so that it falls down according to what we have said.
And then heal the wound with the other treatment of wounds until it is healed.
Chapter .lxxxvi.
Of a swollen hernia.
In this hernia I have not seen anyone who has been cured by the treatment with iron.
And the first say that it is done just as we have recommended in the hernia that is caused by wine; which is that you sew up the vessels around the cut with ease, and then dry up the abscess in the middle of it by opening it up so that the vessels are closed off.
And heal the wound according to what we have said until it is healed.
Chapter .lxxxvii.
Of the rupture that occurs in the intestines.
Sometimes a rupture occurs in the intestines as we have said, and the location protrudes.
And do not give the patient any cause for the intestines to become wrapped around each other; and if they do, it is very little; and return them to their original position within a few hours.
But if time passes by with this, there is a tear in the membrane where the intestine descends into the membrane; and it happens because of the extension of the membrane which is in the intestines as we have said, which causes it to be stretched and softened, and then the location becomes abscessed and protrudes.
And its cure is by cauterization just as we have described in the narrative of it.
And sometimes it is cured by iron in this way: and the patient lies on his back between your hands, and then you dry up the location of the rupture of the abscesses that protrude with a cut according to its width, about three fingers wide.
And then strengthen the tough white membrane below the scrotum so that it is exposed.
And then take a stick and place it on the protruding location of the membrane, and press it against the bone of the belly.
And then cut the two protruding locations on the end of the membrane with a stick, and adjust them by sewing up one of those to the other.
And then pull out the end of the stick, and do not cut into the membrane at all, nor extend the swelling, nor any other cause that you may know in the cure of intestinal hernia.
And then heal it with the cure of wounds, and when you have sewn up the threads, cleanse it and restore the wound until it is consolidated; for the membrane is contracted and the protrusion of the rupture is not adjusted.
And cauterization is better in this location, for it is closer to health.
Chapter .lxxviii.
Of the softening of the scrotum.
Many times the scrotum in some men becomes softened because of the softness of the flesh that is between it, and they fail to guard against it.
Therefore it is necessary that he who is treated in this way makes the patient lie on his back and raises his scrotum up according to its shape, and then cut off all of the softened skin on top of the natural membrane; and then sew together the two lips.
And if you want, cut off the excess of the softened membrane at the beginning with three or four incisions and with a firm suturing.
And then sew up between the sutures; and then heal by the cure of the other wounds until it is healed and the threads fall out.
Chapter .lxxxix.
Of emasculation.
Know that emasculation in our law is prohibited, but I have been asked to remember it in this book; and it is not necessary for me to remember it except in two ways, of which one is so that it may be in the knowledge of the doctor when he is questioned about it, who knows its cure when it occurs; and the other way is that we sometimes have a need for emasculation of other animals for our own sake, as with horses, and cows, and pigs, and similar to beasts.
And therefore I say that emasculation is done in two ways: either by piercing, or by cutting at the incision.
But in that which is done by piercing, the way of the operation is that we make the beast lie in water so that its testicles are softened and hang down, and that they are pierced. And then take them with your hand so that they are resolute and do not protrude below the touch.
But in emasculation done by cutting and incision, see that you have the beast and press the scrotum of its testicles with your left hand.
And then tie up the suspensory ligament, and cut over each orifice so that two orifices are cut through.
And then sew up those which you have just now cut. And do not let any cause fall upon those of the membrane, except the thin membrane which is over the veins.
And this method of castration is better, which is done by constriction, for strong constriction will leave no cause in the testicles that the animal should desire to copulate.
Then treat the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 70:
Of the cure for hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men occurs in two ways: the first is when a growth appears in the space between the testicles, a kind of female glandular tissue.
And sometimes urine flows from it, from the area between the testicles.
But in women, there is only one type: the clitoris on the vagina is like two testicles of a man, a little smaller at the entrance, and like the foreskin of a man, and two testicles.
And the cure is in three ways: two from men and one from women. And it is necessary to cut out the tight flesh so that the moisture of that flows out, and then cure that with the cure for other wounds.
And in the second type of men from which urine flows and is located in the space between the testicles, there is neither cure nor operation for it.
Chapter 71:
Of an abnormal growth and突出flesh from causes in women.
A mole is a growth on natural causes that is tightly bound and is caused by constriction, and in some women it spreads like it does in men and affects coitus.
Therefore, if you have an excess of moles, cut them with your hand or with a pair of scissors.
And do not cut all the way through, especially at the root of the hair, lest it cause bleeding.
Then cure that with the cure for wounds until it is healed.
But a growth is flesh that grows in the womb of the mother and fills it up, and often appears at the entrance like a tail; therefore, if we cut it as we would a mole, then we should cure it until it is healed.
Chapter 72:
Of the cure for hernia.
A hernia is when the clitoris of a woman is not perforated or has a small hole in it. And it can be natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to an injury that preceded it, and it is caused by tightly bound flesh or a thin membrane or membrane.
And it occurs in the area of the womb or on the ribs or the upper abdomen or lower abdomen, and it is prohibited from coitus and pregnancy and menstruation, and often prohibits urination.
And the diagnosis of it is made by examination of the midwife if the swelling is obvious, or if not obvious then you should touch it with your fingers or the palm of your hand.
But if the swelling is due to a thin membrane and is close to both labia, then you should cut and tear it apart.
And you shall pause over both labia with your fingers, and then pause the tips of your fingers against the flesh on both sides.
And let the woman be on her back with her legs extended and spread the two labia with force so that the thin membrane is torn and the swelling is opened.
And then take wool and soak it in oil and place it over the wound, and bind it with a bandage every day so that the wound does not close up again.
But if the membrane is thick and strong, then you should cut it with a sharp knife or with the blade of a myrtle twig.
But if the swelling is due to flesh, then suspend it with a pair of scissors and cut it.
And you shall have the medicines that stop bleeding without biting, like astringents and dragon's blood and honey, bound with egg white.
And then administer a wide leaden bandage so that the wound does not heal quickly.
And let her keep it for several days and administer warm water.
Then it will be healed with the other cure of consolidation until it is healed.
And sometimes they occur in the womb due to the birth of other flesh, and then you should cut it according to this manner. But if it is due to scrofula and the scrofula is not caused by any contrary condition, then do not use iron in any way.
Chapter 73:
Of the cure for hemorrhoids and of a tail and of red bouton that occur in the clitoris of women.
Hemorrhoids are an appearance of the openings of many veins from which they flow continuously, and with age hemorrhoids grow larger.
And I have already written in the division of those and their signs, and said thus those that received cure and those who did not receive cure.
Therefore I say that hemorrhoids and theyls when they are in the area of the womb and do not appear to be caused by feeling, then in those there should not be cure with iron.
But those which are in the openings of the womb over which there is sensation, they are to be cured.
And let the woman be in a sitting position and then extend it with the fingers or with rough cloth, and cut it at the roots.
And then sprinkle over it some of the powdered iron without biting, like cassia and similar to those.
And then let her walk for an hour, and then place that in tepid water.
And if the bleeding continues, then let her drink a decoction of sumac and myrobalan and pomegranate rinds and similar things.
And then take wheat flour and cook that with honey and bitter wine and make a plaster of it and place it over her abdomen.
And if the bleeding is scanty, let it be; but if not, let two leeches adhere to her breasts and to the nipples their incision.
And then take wool and soak it in the juice of henbane or in the juice of henna or in the juice of walnut and in bitter wine, and let the wound be bound with it until it is healed.
And cure that until it is healed.
Chapter 74:
Of accidental piercing of the clitoris.
Many types of scrofula occur in the womb, like a hard scrofula and scrofula with teeth and an ulcerous one and suppurating and with scabs and abscesses and hemorrhoids and others. And I have already written about these illnesses and their signs and their cures in the division.
And let you listen in this treatise of scrofula caut which appears in the womb when the scrofula is caused by cold humors, and if you want to know in what manner its operation is done with iron.
Therefore consider whether the pain of the scrofula in its beginning is acute with percussion and phlegm and fever, and if it has a burning sensation and if you feel that over it, then do not pierce it, and cure it with what helps in preventing the acuteness of the accidents.
And then you must make the woman lie down on a bed that has two pillows; recline on her back and straighten her feet to the lower part of her belly, let her thighs be spread apart, place her arms below her ears, and tie each limb to what is convenient.
Then the midwife should stand on the right side and administer the instrument with which the opening of the uterus is dilated, the shape of which will depend on the individual case.
And when you want to administer this instrument, place your thumb on the uterus of the woman, and what enters the uterus from the instrument should not be larger than the uterus itself and lead the patient. But if the instrument is larger than the opening of the uterus, then you should apply powder to the tissue of the opening of the uterus so that the insertion of any instrument into the uterus is prohibited.
And you should apply the grease that runs along the instrument from above, and the person administering the instrument should turn the grease within as the opening of the uterus is dilated.
And when the fetus appears, and is touched by hand and becomes soft, then you should dry its head with a sponge on one side.
And when the placenta is delivered, then you should place a sponge soaked in rose oil or oil with some styptic in the wound and place the calcium in the incision in the uterus.
And after delivering the placenta, place clean wool soaked in water over the uterus, and in which are crushed mallows.
Then it should be healed after two days with ointment that is suitable for this purpose until it is healed.
And sometimes the uterus and wound are washed with water and honey, and then with water in which is crushed rhubarb or long pepper, and then return to the ointment.
And if the wound is deep in the uterus, then you should be prohibited from curing it with iron, but treat that as we have said in the division.
Chapter .lxxv.
To teach midwives how to treat unborn babies when they are born according to an unnatural shape.
It is necessary that the midwife know at the beginning the shape of natural childbirth by its signs, and it is that when you see the woman express herself from the lower parts and desire to breathe the air, and over that is what is above her, and hastens the ejection of the baby, then you know that this birth is according to a natural shape, and the ejection of it is over his head, and the second one with that or suspended or hanging from the umbilical cord.
Therefore when you see these signs, then the belly of her should be compressed so that the embryo descends gently, when it descends over his head, then the second one comes after him, and is cleaned from those superfluities with good cleaning.
But that which is different from this birth is unnatural and blameworthy, for when the baby exits over its feet and the body of her exits before her head and her feet, and her hand, or at her leg. or the head of her exits and her hand, or at her belly, and strongly it is turned on his neck, and similar to the shapes of her blameworthy.
It is necessary that the midwife be wise and subtle in all those causes, and that she guard against error and deception.
And you should show all the figures of these, and what skill is in these so that it be signified by that and be established on that.
When the baby exits over his head by natural effort, and he is violent on the woman and the delivery for her is difficult, then you should make him cease, or that the women hold him, and evaporate the heat from him with fenugreek powder and with moist oils.
Then the midwife should insert her finger with a small sponge and split it with that the second one, or dry her with her fingernail within so that it removes what is in her of moisture. And compress the belly of the woman so that the fetus exits.
But if it does not exit, then you should smear the woman with a poultice of pith and a poultice of fenugreek with chamelee.
And then command him, the one who is compressing, that she be pressed and make her sneeze with some medicine; and take his mouth and nose for an hour, for the fetus will exit immediately.
And if both hands of the fetus are exited at the beginning, then you should reduce those with little ease little by little. But if it does not obey the insertion, then place the woman on a bed and lift her feet up, and then shake the bed gently so that she doesn't fall because of the shaking.
And if the hands are not bent back and the fetus is dead, then insert those and pull the limbs of the fetus or tie the body to his hand with a cloth and pull that equally, for he will exit immediately.
When the fetus exits over his feet, then you should push those up on him, and then turn the fetus gently, and then grab one of his feet and pull those gently little by little.
But when he exits into the thighs, then you command him to expel, and make her sneeze with medicine, for he will exit if God wills it.
And if it is not exited with what we have recommended, then you should return the fetus little by little to how you place that according to a natural shape, for he will exit immediately with gentle ejection.
And if it is prohibited by all that we have recommended, then take a poultice of mallows and dissolved gum, and beat them all in the mortar with good beating, and apply it to what the heat of the woman is, at the bottom of her belly. Then make her sweat in warm water so that she attains the hippocratic crisis.
And when you see that his lower parts are loosened, then you should give him a fumigation of myrrh and place that below him. And when she has been given the fumigation for an hour, then make her cease on a bed, and then make her sneeze and open her mouth, and lift that, and compress the lower part of her belly gently, for the fetus will exit immediately.
The feet hang down latitude-wise from one of his hands. Let him try to pull it back with his hand; but if he cannot, then let the woman stand up and walk around.
And if she cannot walk then let her lie down on the bed and hit her thighs with a violent blow, and administer poultices which have been moistened with mucilage.
And if the child has been delivered then let her sit up and work on pulling back the hand; and straighten out the feet according to their natural shape; make the woman sneeze and order him to press himself in until he is completely expelled.
The child is hanging over her mother's shoulder, with his hands and the surface of his body spread out. That the midwife should have the hand of the child and gradually turn him over little by little; and that this is made easier.
And when it is and how much it is wrapped up, then place over the navel of the child that which we have recommended of oil and mucilage.
And then command him to suckle little by little and when you have done that let her lie down on one side and command him to be pressed in; and make the woman sneeze with some medicine. The preparation of the exit of the fetus is over the side.
When they are going to be horrified by the mother according to this method, consider and then insert your finger inside so that it is evacuated of moisture.
And if the child is suspended over the face and neck, then insert your finger into the navel so that he is not retained and delayed.
And then press the child towards the parts inside as you pause that according to what the midwife wants; and order the woman to press herself in several times and he will be expelled easily with the exit hanging down, God willing.
The exit of twins or many fetuses. Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four, but that is strange and difficult; but they are caused by nature and do not live.
And count those, now that they are multiplied, one second, and they are separated by the placenta; distinguish between them in the umbilical cord of each of them. And sometimes they are expelled thus with an easy natural exit, and sometimes with an exit not to be laughed at as we have recommended.
And if they are difficult to deliver and arrive at that to which we have said about the non-natural figures, then you cure them thus as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is subtle and does what she does with facility and subtlety, and with tardiness, and it is worked on according to all the figure as it is prepared for him by bringing about health.
Remembrance of that which is formed in the womb from embryos and abortions.
Sometimes they are formed in the womb as one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and even ten, and I have indeed seen that a woman who aborts may have six, and another ten of them, the cause of which was discovered by the glorious wise ones through measurement.
And all that being said that it should be in the science of the midwife how strong they are at that small thing and then pause at that with which she does that.
Chapter .lxxvi.
On the extraction of the child when it is dead.
When you treat the dead child with what we have said in the division of medicine and it is not expelled out, and you must use incision with the hand; then consider if the woman is of healthy nature and has none of the accidents by which she is thought to be in danger of loss.
Then let the woman lie on her back on her side with her head inclined down and her thighs raised up.
And the minister should hold that in two parts or be tied in the bed so that the body of the child does not extend due to the extraction of the child.
And then you moisten the mouth of the mother with oiled and moistened mucilage of altaea, and of fenugreek, and of linseed.
And then the midwife applies her hand with those oils and mucilages, and then inserts her hand with facility in the mother, and then encloses her hand around the place where the nails are in the child.
And convenient places for that: then consider if the child is prepared to descend over his head; and then you place the nails in his hollows or in the neck, or in the mouth, or on the palate, or under the beard, or in the furcula, or in places near the ribs, or under the armpits.
But if the descent is over his feet then in the sole of the foot, or in the middle of the back.
And have the nail with the right hand and pause the curve of it in that place which is between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the hand with facility and place the nail in some of those places which we have said, so that he comes to the desired cause.
And then pause and place in the opposition of him another nail, or the third if it is necessary, so that there is an attraction alike, and not an extension according to its uprightness only.
And the hand is stretched out to all parts so that the exit of him is drawn away just as it is done in teeth extraction.
And let the extension be made smooth in that which is between them so that what is retained is released; and if any part of him is retained, then let the midwife moisten his fingers with oil and insert that medicine and turn him around so that he who is retained is released.
Then if the exit of the child is drawn out, then the nails are transferred to another place where there is an opening; and do that so that all the child is expelled.
But if the hand is drawn out in front of the other and it is not possible to reduce that by the contraction of him, then let the cloth be wrapped around that; and then extract that so that all is expelled, and insert that or in the joint of the hand or in the armpit.
And thus you do in the other hand and in both feet.
But if the head of the child is large, or there happens to him contraction in the exit, or it is in his head tightly bound, then let the midwife insert between his fingers aspidium spinosum and split the head and extract the water, or gouge that with an instrument which is named “alundat”, the form of which will come from the forms of other instruments in the chapter which is next.
And do likewise if the child is of a large head by nature: and then let that be inserted with an instrument, or that be taken up with an alundum just as we have said; and then extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is drawn out and is bound because of the furcula, then it is split so that the moisture which is in the feet is poured out.
But if he is not complicated nor obstinate against exit, then you insert the head just as you can.
And if the insides of the abdomen are pustular or are edematous, then you must pierce that which allows the moisture inside to flow out.
But if the pain is in their feet, then the attraction is slight and the direction towards the mouth of the mother is also slight.
But if it is constricted from the abdomen to the feet, then you must extract that with a cloth which you have wrapped around your hand, and split the abdomen and the feet so that what is inside flows out.
But if the other members are cut off and the head is turned, then the midwife should insert her left hand; but if the mouth of the mother is open, then she should insert her hand into the anus, surround that with her hand, and draw that towards the mouth of the mother, and then insert a finger or two inside it and draw it out with those.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted by pustular heat which comes from within, then you must not put anything in there; instead, administer infusions of moist, fatty causes. And give ointments; and follow the patient with waters that soften and moisten.
And if it is in their side, then if possible, it should be sutured; and what we said about the living fetus should also be administered.
And if that is not possible, then it should be incised with a sharp object and extracted.
And make sure to leave no cause inside the womb.
And once you have completed all of your operations, then administer what we said about the treatment in the pustular heat which comes from within the mother.
And if bleeding occurs, then use astringent waters and administer the other treatment.
And I once saw a woman whose belly contained a dead fetus, and inside that was another fetus alive, and the other was a dead fire. A long time afterwards, an abscess appeared in her womb; and something inside became swollen so that the heat opened up and began to vomit fire.
And I was called to heal it, and I treated her for a long time, yet the wound did not heal.
Then I applied to it some strong-attracting ointments, and extracted an os from it, and then after a few days, another; and I was very astonished, for there are no bones in the belly.
And so I thought that they were bones of the dead fetus.
Then I opened the wound and extracted from her many bones; the woman remained in the same disposition, and she lived like this for a long time, vomiting fire occasionally.
And I did not consider this strange, for there is knowledge and aid in this so that the doctor with his hands can administer a cure.
Of the forms of instruments which are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of the incision by which the mother is opened:
This is the form of the string which holds the lips together, to this joining there are two virtues at both ends of two strings. But this virtue must be more subtle than the string, and it should be made either from gut or from wood-pulp.
And each wood should be as thick as two fingers and the width of both ends of the strings is one finger; and the length of each is half a palm, and in the middle of the strings there are two joints of that wood, which are already tied together, the length of each is about a palm and a little more, and the width of each is about two fingers or a little more.
And these two additions should be inserted into the mother's mouth so that she is opened by them when you turn the two prescribed virtues.
Other similar form, but more subtle and lighter:
It should be made of gut or wood-pulp according to the appearance of forceps. But at the end of it there should be two additions like pliers, and the length of each addition is about a palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open the mother with them, then you should make her lie on her back, opening what is between her thighs. And then open your hand with the instrument like you do with forceps, according to the amount that you want of the opening of the mother' mouth so that the midwife can do what she wants.
The form of the incision which the ancients described:
Form of the impulsion by which the fetus is pushed:
Form of the incision by which the large head is cut
And it is like forceps whose teeth are in the end, like this, and sometimes an incision is made long like this with forceps, like this, whose teeth are like the teeth of a saw with which it is cut and incised. Form of the small incision:
Form of a nail having one spike:
Form of a nail having two spikes:
Form of a spatula having two ends by which the head is cut:
Form of two wide spatulas:
All those instruments are exercised, and when they are more numerous and prepared by the artisans, it is easier for them to operate and better for men because of their quantity.
And you must have those instruments, for the necessity of them is inexcusable.
Of extraction of the placenta:
When the placenta is retained after childbirth, then you must command the midwife to hold her heel, and then make her sneeze with a handkerchief, and press your hand over her mouth and nose, and if it comes out through that, good.
And if not, then take a jar and pierce a hole in its lid, and place herbs which burn the mouth of the mother, like calamus and rue and anise and camomile and aromatic myrrh and cassia wood and santal wood. All of these herbs or some of them should be submerged in water in the jar, and place that over the fire.
And then place a tube of reed in the mother's mouth, and hold it there so that the vapor goes into the cavity of the mother.
And then make her sneeze as we said before, and let the placenta come out with velocity.
But if this treatment is applied and it has not worked, then command the midwife to submerge her left hand in sesame oil or in myrrh milk, and then insert that into the vagina and press with it the placenta, and when she has found the placenta, extract it little by little according to how the mother does not suffer a violent attraction. After that let it be turned to the right and left side with facility.
And if the mother' mouth is constricted, we have recommended the cure with snuffing and with medicine from the jar with herbs.
But if it is not eliminated with all the causes we have mentioned, then beware of over-exerting yourself in an attempt to draw it out, but rather ensure that what comes out of the mouth and into the mother's breast goes to the woman's thigh; then anoint the area with ointment and tetrachemical remedy. For this will cause it to rot in a few days, become dissolved, and be eliminated.
But when it rots, a bad odor rises to the head and stomach, and that hurts the patient; so make sure to administer sub-fomentation and suitable remedies for this.
But some of the Ancients have already experimented with sub-fomentation using nasea and dry figs.
Here is a way to use the instrument by which the woman is sub-fomentated because of the retention of menses and the secondina:
It should be made of glass or copper.
And the narrow end should be placed in the vagina and the wider end over the fire; then the sub-fomentation should be placed over the embers of the fire.
And let that which is within be consumed by the sub-fomentation and repeat another [dosage].
For the treatment of the anus of a non-perforated infant:
Most newborn infants and their anuses are not perforated; they have thin and elastic skin. Therefore, the midwife should use her finger to perforate that thin skin; and if not, perforate it with a sharp spatula, and beware of touching the clitoris.
Then place wool soaked in wine and oil over that; and cure that with ointment until it is healed.
But if you are afraid it is closed, then insert a cannula for a few days and remove it when the infant wants to defecate.
And sometimes the anus is closed by a coagulation of plasma or of pus; therefore that coagulation should be incised and then cured with what we have said about the cure and the plug.
For the cure of the fistulas which go inside:
The fistulas that go inside at the beginning of the anus discharge pus; they have a node and are thick, and they can be found near the anus or in the space of one side.
And it is a fistula or many.
And when that node becomes old and discharges thin white or rotten fluid, then some of these fistulas penetrate in some places.
And those which penetrate are known by what comes out of them through the orifices and through windiness; and sometimes the patient vomits it, and often it comes out of them with worms.
And sometimes these fistulas penetrate into the bladder and into the vagina; and some of them penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the hip socket.
And that in which the penetrating fistula is known to have entered the anus but not exited is when you insert your finger into the anus and press a thin rod of copper or iron into the fistula when it is swollen.
But if it is swollen, then insert a thin rod of lead or horse hair into it until you feel the rod or the hair in your finger.
And if you don't feel it at all or if there is no sign of excretion or worms or windiness, then know that it is not penetrating; then return to the cure.
And when the fistula penetrates into the bladder or into the vagina, then its sign is the excretion of urine from it and the prohibition of that by applying medicine to it until the place is healed.
But if it penetrates into the joint of the thigh or into the hip socket and there is pain in the circle around it, then its sign is that the rod goes inside there if there is no swelling in the bone, and pain in the circle around the affected area; and when there is pus, heat, and when medicine does not help it or heal it.
And in all penetrating fistulas there is no cure for sure; and the cure of those is work and skill of doctors over which we have written.
But in that which is not penetrating and does not become old, healing is expected with iron according to what you have written and that which has already been tried.
And let the patient lie on his side over your knee and raise his legs up onto you, with his thighs slanted towards his belly; then insert a rod of lead or iron into the fistula until you know where the rod goes in.
And if he feels pain around his neck, then let you insert your finger into his neck.

But some say it heals in some people with a fever.

On stitching up hemorrhoids in which blood flows in their incision.
Hemorrhoids come in two ways, because they are either between the anus looking like warts, or they are like the grease of hair. And they are small and large, and the blood flows from them constantly, and they are located, and on the edges of the anus.
But those that are outside the anus are according to the months of little humidity, from which flows a yellow water or a little blood with continuous flesh, and they are according to the color of the flesh.
And the treatment for that which is inside the anus is that you order the patient to sit and squeeze so that the anus dries and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you cut and grab with your nails or whatever you have those with your fingernail, and then you pierce them at their roots.
But if the nails are not in them due to their moisture and softness, then take them with a rough cloth or with a stick or with a piece of wool, and pull them out with your teeth, and then insert them and spread over them some powders mixed together at the incision, so that they are as cautery; or cauterize them according to what is preceded in the chapter on cauterizing. And then heal them with the other treatment until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey the exit, then you crucify the patient with a small cross made of wood, and wash him with the water that is in his anus and which causes the exit more quickly when he squeezes himself.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then the cause of them is leanness, and it is that you grab them with your fingernail, or grab them with your nail, and insert them, and then heal them with what we have said until they are healed.

And do this to all of them, and leave one not sewn up, so that the excess blood flows out from it.

Of care of the sores:
You have already said in the division of the care of sores what was proper for the book, and I say thus is the care of those with hand and medicines according to the complement.
Therefore I say that sores are various according to what is caused by the sores and according to the place on which occurred the sores.
And the causes why many times sores are caused are thus as hitting of stone, or piercing with spear or with knife, or hitting with lance or with club, or with arrow, or the like to those causes.
But the sores which are in the parts of the body are thus as sore that fell upon the head, or neck, or feet, or belly, or thigh, and the like to those of the members.
And I am recounting the care of some sores so that you understand that reasoning and rule about the other sores.
And I will begin of the sores of head simple, for the memory of the compounded will come to the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore I say that when it happens in the head simple sore and there is no fracture, then consider: if it is by hitting of stone or the like, and the tendon has been broken only and there is great sore and you fear about that patient a tumor, then you cool it and take phlebotomy of the cephalic vein at once, and do not delay that; and draw off blood from that according to the amount of its strength if no other cause prohibits phlebotomy, mostly if the blood which has come out of the sore is little.
And let the phlebotomy be on the contrary side from the sore party; and beware of the patient's replection and of wine and heavy food.
But if because of the minor any cause prohibits that, then it is diminished from food and do not approach meat or wine.
And place upon the sore, if there happens to it tumor cautery, cut cotton steeped in rose oil or wine in which is steeped;
But if it is secure from tumor cautery, then place upon the sore, if it is recent with its blood and the air has not changed that powder which I recounted earlier, then apply it small;
And if the air has already changed that, then place upon some ointment until it is healed.
But if the sore is large or it is by piercing with knife and the like, and its lips are not sewed together by threads, then sew those together according to how I recounted of their sewing.
But if the sore is uncovered of bone and nerve, and there is not retention of it except a small suspension, then insert that and let the sore be cared by medicines and restore the meat after in place of tendon, and command the patient that he abstains from food in which is coarseness: heads and forms of meat and the like to them, until it is composite.
And if you find in the tendon putrefaction and it does not adhere to bone, then insert all that putrid and throw that, and let it be cared.
But if in these sores is artery or vein from which flows blood and it has not been cut off by medicines, then you press upon the artery, and if you find that uncut, then you insert that with spatula, or ligature that; and if necessity prompts you to do that which I have recounted, then cauterize until the blood is abscised.
And if these sores are simple and small, then the cause of them is dryness; thus that you powder upon those this powder, for when the air changes that before which.
And the manner of the powder is this: take oil of eggs yolk one, of blood of dragon two parts, of milk not-extinguished three parts; let it be all dry and sifted, and of that be the sore filled, and let it be bound by good constriction until it lies over that healing, and let the blood coagulate.
And let it be tightened above that with powders and let her lie thus until it is healed, for there is not inherited of it the medicine until it is healed.
And at times do that alone cautery when you have not at hand eggs and blood of dragon;
And do this meteyssa operation in great sores when it seems that it should be placed upon them and be tight, and so sores recent with its blood, which the air has not altered;
And if the air has altered them, and especially when it is in summer time, then it is not intent to the position of this powder, but afterwards cure those with that which I have recounted, thus that you place upon those some ointments digested, or that you place upon those poultices of flour of barley with water and honey until they are cooked; and let them be cared by the other care until they are healed.
But if it happens with the sore fracture of bone, and is small, then you draw that out with tweezers.
